  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_affbfcdc-dd78-4131-95a9-88a84c30349b'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();

<span id="freeTextContainer8296698270048700489">In the medieval and fantastic realm of Tortall, Keladry of Mindelan is the first girl to take advantage of the decree that permits females to train for knighthood.   <span id="freeText8296698270048700489" style="display:none">In the medieval and fantastic realm of Tortall, Keladry of Mindelan is the first girl to take advantage of the decree that permits females to train for knighthood. Up against the traditional hazing of pages and a grueling schedule, Kel faces only one real roadblock: Lord Wyldon, the training master of pages and squires. He is absolutely against girls becoming knights. So while he is forced to train her, Wyldon puts her on probation for one year. It is a trial period that no male page has ever had to endure and one that separates the good natured Kel even more from her fellow trainees during the tough first year. But Kel Is not a girl to underestimate, as everyone is about to find out...</span>

<span class='communityAnswererName'>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Yes. It's set in the same world, but 10 years after the Song of the Lioness series is complete. About 5 years after the Immortals Quartet. While it's <a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Yes. It's set in the same world, but 10 years after the Song of the Lioness series is complete. About 5 years after the Immortals Quartet. While it's not focused on Alanna, she does show up as well as some other familiar faces. I highly recommend reading the Immortals Quartet first though, as the first book references events from that series pretty heavily.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/1578092-the-blurb-describes-alanna-s-first-book">The blurb describes Alanna&#39;s first book almost exactly. What is the difference between these two stories of pages going through tough training?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_1578092'><a id="like_count_community_question_1578092" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/1578092?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">1 like</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F153784.First_Test">like</a></span>

<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/4167919-zoe"><img alt="" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_100x100-6433b08cbe793211f55e184d39e84c4d.png" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/4167919-zoe">Zoe</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Alanna's story was focused around her hiding her identity as a girl from the rest of the knights, her reluctance to practice her magic, and an eventua<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Alanna's story was focused around her hiding her identity as a girl from the rest of the knights, her reluctance to practice her magic, and an eventual love story. Kel's story differs because everyone knows she is a girl, so the central conflict is her proving that she is good enough to be a knight despite her gender. Also, she doesn't have magic or a love story.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/23488799" />
    <a title="Allison" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1122115-allison"><img alt="Allison" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1303844711p2/1122115.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/23488799?book_show_action=true">Jun 01, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Allison" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Allison" href="/user/show/1122115-allison">Allison</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1122115-allison?shelf=tamora-pierce">tamora-pierce</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1122115-allison?shelf=genre-high-fantasy">genre-high-fantasy</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer23488799" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16604412112706279711">Recently I decided to reread all of Tamora Pierce's books, because, well, it's been too long since I read them. For her Lioness Quartet, Circle of Magic books, and The Immortals series, I was refreshing my memory, but with the Protector of the Small series, it was almost like reading them for the first time. I read this series only once, when I was a preteen, and I had honestly forgotten just how much I love Kel.<br/><br/>At first glance, the story of Keladry of Mindalen seems like a rewrite of Tamora Pie</span>
  <span id="freeText16604412112706279711" style="display:none">Recently I decided to reread all of Tamora Pierce's books, because, well, it's been too long since I read them. For her Lioness Quartet, Circle of Magic books, and The Immortals series, I was refreshing my memory, but with the Protector of the Small series, it was almost like reading them for the first time. I read this series only once, when I was a preteen, and I had honestly forgotten just how much I love Kel.<br /><br />At first glance, the story of Keladry of Mindalen seems like a rewrite of Tamora Pierce's first series, The Lioness Quartet, which features a spunky girl named Alanna who dresses as a boy in order to train as a knight. When I read the books years ago, I loved them, and saw Alanna as a hero, but now, as a college freshman, I see her character a little differently. In my opinion, Alanna chooses to be a knight as an alternative to learning to be a lady. Although she is a tomboy, she does not choose Knighthood because she loves to fight and longs to protect her country- she does it in an attempt to escape. From the start she is helped by the heir to the throne, her manservant (a trained knight in his own right), and the goddess herself. Although she has honor, Alanna is spiteful with a terrible temper, and is able to use her magical gift to help her through the worst of times.<br /><br />In contrast, we have Keladry of Mindalen, who is allowed to apply as a page without concealing her gender. But by being honest about her sex, Keladry makes herself vulnerable to all sorts of sexism and abuse. Because she is a girl, Kel is forced to undergo a one year "probationary period" (which is not required of boy pages) so that she may prove herself. During this first year, Kel is constantly bullied and experiences hazing and abuse the likes of which Alanna never saw. However, Kel quickly proves, against all odds, that she is as good, if not better, than the boys.<br /><br />Unlike Alanna, Kel knows that she wants to fight. She doesn't want glory, thanks or praise, but rather, seeks her shield so that she may protect those who cannot protect themselves. Kel has no real help from her idol, Alanna, no manservant to help her through, and no magical gift to fall back on. Instead, she uses her strength and determination to prove herself to even the most skeptical trainers. <br /><br />After reading this book I realized, with a start, that I absolutely adore Kel. Although some reviews may disagree, I believe that Tamora Pierce has improved upon her Lioness Quartet with the Protector of the Small Series.<br /><br />Hooray for Kel!</span>
  <a data-text-id="16604412112706279711" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/894739554" />
    <a title="Rachel E. Carter" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29482005-rachel-e-carter"><img alt="Rachel E. Carter" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1512593159p2/29482005.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/894739554?book_show_action=true">Mar 28, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachel E. Carter" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachel E. Carter" href="/user/show/29482005-rachel-e-carter">Rachel E. Carter</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer894739554" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9911075342598374810"><b>No review I could ever write would do this book (or series) justice.</b> <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1402158529ra/9901254.gif' width='400' height='400' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>This series to me is the pinnacle of Tamora Pierce's career. She had many wonderful books but the emotional and physical turmoil her protagonist Kel goes through to earn her knighthood is nothing that I have ever experienced in another YA book. Kel perseveres against every trial imaginable, and while at times she can seem a bit too mature (she's only 10 in this one!), she is unique and refreshing in a world of cliche. She is wh</span>
  <span id="freeText9911075342598374810" style="display:none"><b>No review I could ever write would do this book (or series) justice.</b> <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1402158529ra/9901254.gif" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This series to me is the pinnacle of Tamora Pierce's career. She had many wonderful books but the emotional and physical turmoil her protagonist Kel goes through to earn her knighthood is nothing that I have ever experienced in another YA book. Kel perseveres against every trial imaginable, and while at times she can seem a bit too mature (she's only 10 in this one!), she is unique and refreshing in a world of cliche. She is what every female warrior should be. And what's more? For once an author cast a tomboy who wasn't secretly some beautiful girl -she was normal, plain, a "Lump."<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1422086486ra/13454618.gif" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>"You won't ask it, but I'll do it anyway, she thought stubbornly. You'll see. I'm as good as any boy. I'm better."</i><br><br>And how about that awesome battle scene:<br><br><i>"Kel promptly forgot her staff lessons. Holding the spear as she would her glaive, she cut with it in a sidelong arc. The weapon's slim razor point sliced through the spidren's chest and arm, releasing a dark spray of blood. Kel reversed the spear and cut back, dragging the blade down. It bit into the spidren at the neck and stuck there as crossbow bolts riddled the immortal."</i><br><br>I'm sorry, how is that not epic? And can I remind you she is only 10 YEARS OLD in this book!<br><br>Now, let's talk about Neal.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/412544.gif" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Her best friend Neal stands out as my <i>favorite</i> side character/best friend in <i>any</i> book I have <i>ever</i> read, and as my Goodreads BFF Monica (who is doing the buddy read with me) pointed out, every single line he says is quotable. He is like Buffy &amp; Kenji &amp; Veronica Mars &amp; an over-dramatizing girlfriend combined, in guy best friend form. Sarcasm &amp; drama to perfection. And he has her back at every turn.<br><br>There is no romance between them in this first book <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[(or really any of them since he never knows about her crush). <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> But this was still me every time he showed up:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1422086732ra/13454626.gif" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Oh, and Joren? This is what needs to happen. Now. You are worse than bloody Malfoy &amp; Joffrey combined. You prat.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1422085727ra/13454482.gif" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Last, but not least, Lord Wyldon. Training master from hell. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Also my Snape. You know, the mean teacher that secretly has the kid's back/wants her to succeed. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1422085727ra/13454483.gif" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>"You will climb this tree every day. If we cannot cure you of fear, you must learn to work despite it, understand?"</i><br><br>If you love YA fantasy read this book now. Tamora Pierce set the standard for strong female warriors in YA. You cannot go wrong. The trials and tribulations Kel faces coupled with the excellent array of characters sets up for an amazing series debut. And since this is a reread I can assure the next books <i>only get better</i>.<br><br><i>Side note: this first book is 100% romance free but it is still impossible to put down -and as someone who lives off romance that is a hard feat to accomplish.</i></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_2194018623" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2194018623" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2194018623?book_show_action=true">Nov 24, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2194018623" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3267694057934720388">This is my first book/series from Tamora Pierce, meaning that I did not read her Song of the Lioness series prior. However, although Alanna, and as I discovered, multiple other characters from the author’s other books in the same world are mentioned, I did not feel as though there was something I was missing to enjoy this particular story.<br/><br/>Actually, because Alanna was mentioned so many times, I now feel very interested in picking Pierce’s Song of the Lioness up. Though it’s true there are some sp</span>
  <span id="freeText3267694057934720388" style="display:none">This is my first book/series from Tamora Pierce, meaning that I did not read her Song of the Lioness series prior. However, although Alanna, and as I discovered, multiple other characters from the author’s other books in the same world are mentioned, I did not feel as though there was something I was missing to enjoy this particular story.<br /><br />Actually, because Alanna was mentioned so many times, I now feel very interested in picking Pierce’s Song of the Lioness up. Though it’s true there are some spoilers in this series, so I would say read it after Song of the Lioness, or before, if it’s not that problematic for you. It wasn’t for me.<br /><br />This is the story of a girl who wants to become a knight. For that to happen, Kel must be trained by the King’s trainer, who dislikes her. Unfortunately, even if girls are technically allowed to become knights now, because of Alanna, they are not exactly welcomed to pursue a path that is believed to be reserved for men by many. <br /><br />But Kel is ready to face the prejudices. She feels it in her bones that this is what she is meant to do. Kel couldn’t have been a better heroine. She is strong, ready to prove to everyone how wrong they are about her. But the best part is, she doesn’t dismiss her feminine side, so as to look ‘‘tougher’’ or ‘‘manly’’. Indeed, she wears dresses from time to time and shows sympathy towards both humans and animals. <br /><br />Because everyone has, at one point or another, been misjudged, underestimated and perhaps bullied or discriminated against, it’s easy for the reader to connect with Kel and invest themselves in the story. <br /><br />I want to point out that Kel is ten years old, but that this is more Young Adult than Middle Grade. It is serious and complex, plus the characters she interacts with are usually much older. <br /><br />Really enjoyed. Eager to read the rest of the series. <br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3267694057934720388" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_26982914" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/26982914" />
    <a title="Kat" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/591761-kat"><img alt="Kat" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1404938632p2/591761.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/26982914?book_show_action=true">Jul 11, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kat" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kat" href="/user/show/591761-kat">Kat</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/591761-kat?shelf=listened">listened</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/591761-kat?shelf=read-more-than-once">read-more-than-once</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/591761-kat?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/591761-kat?shelf=march2011">march2011</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer26982914" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3300995196177518599">I started this series with the thought that it was going to be a do over of Pierce's previous, successful Alanna the Lioness Quartet, which followed a girl (named Alanna, of course) who dressed like a boy and took her twin brother's place in page training while he took her place in magic school (not dressed as a girl). The four books of that quartet follow her progress from page, to squire, to knight and king's champion--with her sex being discovered along the way. I was pleasantly surprised to </span>
  <span id="freeText3300995196177518599" style="display:none">I started this series with the thought that it was going to be a do over of Pierce's previous, successful Alanna the Lioness Quartet, which followed a girl (named Alanna, of course) who dressed like a boy and took her twin brother's place in page training while he took her place in magic school (not dressed as a girl). The four books of that quartet follow her progress from page, to squire, to knight and king's champion--with her sex being discovered along the way. I was pleasantly surprised to find that not only does Pierce give Keladry her own unique strong personality and story, but also that in some ways I enjoyed Keladry's story more than Alanna's. <br /><br />Keladry's struggle to be the first openly female page in Tortall strikes me as being braver than Alanna's secret struggles. Being openly female Keladry has to deal with all the aggression and contempt of the males who don't want to her to succeed, as well as a blatant double standard (even though the law since Alanna's time says that girls can train as pages, Keladry is put on probation for her first term).<br /><br />On top of that, where Alanna has the help of her magical powers and the Mother Goddess of her universe, Keladry works through her problems on her own.<br /><br />Definitely a girl empowering story!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3300995196177518599" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_34273709" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/34273709" />
    <a title="Kogiopsis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1462364-kogiopsis"><img alt="Kogiopsis" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1494267218p2/1462364.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/34273709?book_show_action=true">Oct 01, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kogiopsis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kogiopsis" href="/user/show/1462364-kogiopsis">Kogiopsis</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer34273709" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10300557857921626345">I am going to save my reminiscing about this series for the third book. Or at least I'm going to try. Some might creep in unnoticed.<br/><br/><br/><br/><br/>First off:<br/>I HATE SPIDRENS I HATE SPIDRENS I HATE SPIDRENS I HATE SPIDRENS.<br/>Spidrens were, actually, the first Immortals I ever read about, because I went straight from the Lioness Quartet to this series. So in the first chapter or so, when Kel finds a spidren <i>biting the heads off kittens</i>, I was deeply disturbed. I still am. What I love about that scene is Kel's react</span>
  <span id="freeText10300557857921626345" style="display:none">I am going to save my reminiscing about this series for the third book. Or at least I'm going to try. Some might creep in unnoticed.<br /><br /><br /><br /><br />First off:<br />I HATE SPIDRENS I HATE SPIDRENS I HATE SPIDRENS I HATE SPIDRENS.<br />Spidrens were, actually, the first Immortals I ever read about, because I went straight from the Lioness Quartet to this series. So in the first chapter or so, when Kel finds a spidren <i>biting the heads off kittens</i>, I was deeply disturbed. I still am. What I love about that scene is Kel's reaction. She wades across a river, gathers a handful of stones, and goes after the monster with only rocks for ammunition. Seriously, this girl is the most badass ten year-old EVER. She's awesome. And she's got a great attitude, to boot: chock full of determination and not about to let traditionalists keep her from becoming a knight. Her motivation to seek knighthood, too, is wonderful; she has a powerful, idealistic belief in chivalry and cannot ignore injustice. This is the kind of pure good straight-up heroine that it's always great to come back to, because you never doubt her; she works for her goals and keeps them always in mind. You know the quip about how a woman has to work twice as hard to be considered half as good as a man? That's the situation Kel is in, and she handles it admirably, right down to making sure everyone remembers that YES, tradition has been broken and there is a girl in their midst by wearing dresses to dinner every night. She is so mature, so confident at such a young age - it's awesome. Rarely does she doubt herself, and she's never ashamed of her gender despite the disadvantage it places her at and the cruelty some of the other pages subject her to because of it.<br /><br />Of course, Kel doesn't do this alone. She gains an excellent group of friends over the course of her year on probation, and that's what helps this series be more than just an Alanna Redux. As Raoul says in Squire, there are several kinds of knights; Alanna is the lone hero type, and Kel is the leader type. It makes sense, then, that while Alanna's story was really focused on her and her adventures, Kel's has a wider supporting cast and they're given plenty of development. (This is, of course, building towards the moment when she needs all of them in Lady Knight.) From quirky Nealan of Queenscove, who's the oldest of the pages and Kel's sponsor, to Kel's year-mate Merric of Hollyrose, they're all great characters and people I would want to be friends with, especially in Kel's position. And they care about her, as evidenced when Neal calls her out for roaming the halls looking for wrongs to set right. It's wonderful to see a tight-knit, realistic group like this portrayed in YA. Kel is no Bella Swan-esque moping loner, and it makes her a far richer character.<br /><br />I'm not really sure where this review is going, or for that matter where it's been. (It's a bit messy up there, I think.) A lot of what I want to say about this series I'm saving for the later books, so for now: If you're new to Tortall, you can start here easily; if you're familiar with the world, this entry in its history is not to be missed. Kel is a heroine to root for and look up to, and if I had my way young girls everywhere would be reading about her adventures instead of about sparklepires and the like.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10300557857921626345" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer11274956540662035675">I liked this book - listened to it as an audio book. It was a quick, fast read. I was mostly interested, but the story was entirely predictable. My biggest problem was that Kel is a 10 year old girl, but at no time did she actually act like it. She was way too mature for her age - both in how she acted, her physical abilities and even how she spoke. It was in no way believable that she was a child. My other gripe is: <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[ I rolled my eyes for the entire ending - the idea that the elit</span></span>
  <span id="freeText11274956540662035675" style="display:none">I liked this book - listened to it as an audio book. It was a quick, fast read. I was mostly interested, but the story was entirely predictable. My biggest problem was that Kel is a 10 year old girl, but at no time did she actually act like it. She was way too mature for her age - both in how she acted, her physical abilities and even how she spoke. It was in no way believable that she was a child. My other gripe is: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I rolled my eyes for the entire ending - the idea that the elite kings guard would take along 20 ten year old kids on a dangerous mission is just absurd.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I did really like the Kel's horse, and the message about standing up for other people who are being bullied. <br /><br />I can mostly let the ending slide, since it is a kids book, and the kids need some kind of heroic ending. I'm not sure if I'll finish with the series. Again - it's not a bad book- I think I would have loved it if I read it when I was 10. I would recommend this one to my 10 year old niece. <br /><br />PS - this cover is terrible. It makes it look like it's about a fire mage or something.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11274956540662035675" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_453885261" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/453885261" />
    <a title="Beth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4063913-beth"><img alt="Beth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1351396026p2/4063913.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/453885261?book_show_action=true">Nov 11, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Beth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Beth" href="/user/show/4063913-beth">Beth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780606328081" href="/book/show/223822.First_Test">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4063913-beth?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4063913-beth?shelf=project-nostalgia">project-nostalgia</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer453885261" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4442031656071082046"><blockquote>Alanna clenched her fists. What was going on? Was Jonathan inclined to give way to the man who'd saved his children?</blockquote>And with that, possibly the stupidest line Pierce has ever written, Kel's story begins. I'm big on details lately, and the introduction is shaky on them. Here are more places the writing is less than precise:<br/><blockquote>The training master absently rubbed the arm in its linen sling. At last he bowed in his chair. "May we compromise, sire?"</blockquote>Maybe that first line is here to show Wyldon's hesitati</span>
  <span id="freeText4442031656071082046" style="display:none"><blockquote>Alanna clenched her fists. What was going on? Was Jonathan inclined to give way to the man who'd saved his children?</blockquote>And with that, possibly the stupidest line Pierce has ever written, Kel's story begins. I'm big on details lately, and the introduction is shaky on them. Here are more places the writing is less than precise:<br /><blockquote>The training master absently rubbed the arm in its linen sling. At last he bowed in his chair. "May we compromise, sire?"</blockquote>Maybe that first line is here to show Wyldon's hesitation before answering Jonathan with the probation proposal. The problem is that his gesture calls to mind the <i>reason</i> for the sling ("hey, remember when my arm was raked by a hurrok while I was saving your kids?") which makes the gesture - not quite absent.<br /><br />And then Alanna stalks out, while: <blockquote>The men stared at the door. Each of them was trying to remember if Alanna the Lioness had ever spoken to Jonathan in that tone before.</blockquote>1. Why would Wyldon care?<br />2. Seriously, this is Alanna. I understand this line is for impact, but it's blunted quite a lot when it's centered on a character who gets mad at people for breakfast. <br /><br />And now, finally, we meet Kel. Here's the thing: I gave this book three stars a few years ago, and I'm going to stick to that, if only so I can illustrate how the series gets progressively better. (Expect four stars for <i>Page</i>, and (gasp) five stars for <i>Squire</i>.) But there are also some reasons three stars are warranted. <i>First Test</i> very much sets the stage. There are a lot of ideas initially laid out without being fully developed, along with the imprecise writing. That starts right away, with Kel's dream.<br /><blockquote>"The short sword is the sword of law. Without it, we are only animals. The long sword is the sword of duty. It is a terrible sword, the killing sword." Her words struck a chord in Kel that left the little girl breathless. She liked the idea that duty was a killing sword.</blockquote>This is an idea Pierce reaches for, but I don't think she ever gets there. Though it would be fascinating if she did, a sort of justification of the violence of this world. <br /><br />Anyway, Kel decides to go even though she'll have to be on probation. I'm tempted to say "Obviously, or there would be no story," but there's a certain worth to stories that baldly lay out sexism and then show how baseless it is. It drives home a point, yes, it's message-oriented, yes; but it also drives Kel as a character because it gives her something to fight, which means it's an important motivation - and we're not so far off from having women in the real world face exactly the same situation, which means it stands as a reminder historically of what things used to be like, in the not-so-distant past.<br /><br />In general, Kel fighting for equal opportunity (much more so than Alanna, who had to hide her identity) means this fantasy world doesn't feel set so long ago. It modernizes this medieval setting. It's an interesting approach.<br /><br />So she marches in and no one will sponsor her. Until Joren steps up, which leads to more sloppy writing. Why would Wyldon refuse Joren as Kel's sponsor? Joren is Wyldon's prize page! And he's okay with <i>Neal?</i> I've read this part three times and it still makes no sense to me. It's too contrived.<br /><br />More importantly, though: NEAL. Neal is so great. Here's where Pierce's best skill, dialogue, really shines:<br /><blockquote>Wyldon's eyebrows snapped together. "You have been told to mind your manners, Page Nealan. I will have an apology for your insolence."<br /><br />Nealan bowed deeply. "An apology for general insolence, your lordship, or some particular offense?"<br /><br />"One week scrubbing pots," ordered Lord Wyldon. "Be silent."<br /><br />Nealan threw out an arm like a player making a dramatic statement. "How can I be silent and yet apologize?"</blockquote>HUMOR: THE SPICE OF LIFE. Neal is funny from the first moment he's introduced, and not only is that entertaining, but it comes to form a cornerstone of his character, and it's consistent, and it's <i>great.</i> (Later on, Duke Baird is said to wear constant mourning for the two sons he lost. If Pierce could've said why, and how, and how that affected Neal, instead of that remaining a throwaway detail...)<br /><br />Alright, onward: Neal takes Kel to the touristy parts of the palace, including the portrait gallery, where Kel gets to see a painting of Jon and Thayet, and Neal gets to introduce the current political situation and position Wyldon as the cranky conservative, angry at Thayet's Kmiri notions (teaching women to fight, teaching everyone to read). How <i>does</i> the guy work for Jon, who not only agrees with Thayet, but also covered for one of the most respected knights in the land while she worked earn her shield and prove that women can fight? <br /><br />The setup in this novel creaks sometimes. <br /><br />(Tangent for a moment: Jon wanting women to train - he sent out heralds ten years before! - clashing with the conservative training master he can't afford to lose, is such a good way of showing the constraints of kingship for a country that's not an absolute dictatorship. That's something this series gets very right: even the best of intentions don't always translate practically.)<br /><br />Kel comes in pretty upset at Jon, because she <i>doesn't</i> know about any of this political jockeying, and she's still awed by his speech after dinner the first day:<br /><blockquote>"Each one of you is a gem, all the more precious because we lost so many. Combined, you are the treasure of the kingdom. Treat yourselves as such... Build your stores of learning. Do it not for yourselves or your teachers or your monarchs. Do it for the kingdom. Do it for us all." He looked over them one last time, nodded briskly, then strode out of the hall. He was gone before any of them remembered to bow.</blockquote>Whewwww. Always loved that part. Jon relies on charisma, sure. But he also shows up and makes them realize they're seen and valued. Kel - grudgingly - recognizes why people are so loyal to him, even calm, pragmatic people like her father. (Incidentally, I'd love to hear more about that.) (Later, Wyldon apparently doesn't know why they have a treaty with the Yamanis - Wyldon, YOU LIVE IN THE PALACE. Why are you allowed to be stupid whenever it's convenient for the plot?)<br /><br />So Kel gets in, gets a sponsor, and goes to her first day of classes, where she almost throws the instructor by mistake. The instructor, by the way, recognizes the throw immediately as one of Nariko's. Hurray for not living in a vacuum! Especially since they're Shang, and they're supposed to, you know, <i>travel.</i> Sometimes the "Tortall is the bestest" stuff, which is really heavy-handed in the Daine series, feels too piled on. There's a better balance here.<br /><br />Kel's story is strongest when it isn't told in isolation, when relevant details from Tortall's past series are brought in to give greater scope to the work. Kel saying she fell down rather than that she got into a fight, for example - "I don't believe falling down is an offense for which I can be expelled." Seriously, lol. And it's so clever to extend the lie like that. It's a perfect excuse.<br /><br />It's a little stupid that only Kel recognizes how violent and stupid the bullying is, by the way. It undermines everyone else's brains. "Tradition!" everyone says. Sure, Neal's Mr. Tradition. That's why he's a first-year page at fifteen. Come on. Neal's my favorite, though, so I don't like when his brains are discounted. He tells Kel, when Kel mentions Daine and Numair, "He's too old for her, you know." YOU TELL 'EM, NEAL. <br /><br />He also tells Kel about Numair turning the Scanran into a tree "just two years ago, at Fief Dunlath" - can someone explain the timeline of the Tortall books to me?? And while you're explaining: why are the servants allowed to break up the pages' fights? Usually they don't mix in at all. And there's a lot of brouhaha about nobles' rights. <br /><br />BUT BACK TO NEAL. <blockquote>"How dare they say the Lioness cheated!" growled Kel. "Great Goddess, she fights ogres and spidrens and armies all the time -"<br /><br />"You really look up to her, don't you?" Neal asked. <br /><br />"She's a hero. She's proved it over and over."<br /><br />"And will go on doing so until the day she dies," he said evenly. "You can smack some people in the face with a haddock and they'll still call it a mouse if a mouse is what they want to see."</blockquote>That's - that's timeless, you know? I've thought about that line for over a decade now, ever since I first read this book.<br /><br />I like when Neal demonstrates he's been to a university, too, and that he's older than Kel. Though maybe it's a little strange he's friends with a ten-year-old? Maybe I'm obsessing over age differences, but it's because Pierce has conditioned me to do so. That's what happens when you pair a sixteen-year-old and her teacher. TOUGH.<br /><br />One more thing Pierce does here: she shows the sexism Kel faces, when she openly goes where no woman has gone before - and she shows the sexism Alanna faces as an adult knight, even after she's proven her heroism, because people latch onto any little thing they can to discount Alanna entirely. Different causes, same effect. I like that.<br /><br />I like that Kel has a lot to learn, and that she's shown learning. Tilting, and swordwork - she humiliates herself sometimes, especially in front of Lord Raoul, which is a great moment. <br /><br />I <i>don't</i> like that Kel gets to be Daine-without-Wild-magic, though. Like, you can just be nice to the animals now, and they'll lead you to monsters? Without being able to reach you through magic? That's having your cake and eating it, too. I'm not a fan.<br /><br />Overall, though? This, warts and all, sets up a series I've enjoyed for a long time. And I can't wait to read further.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4442031656071082046" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_602327878" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/602327878" />
    <a title="Bridget Mckinney" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6915631-bridget-mckinney"><img alt="Bridget Mckinney" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1492735651p2/6915631.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/602327878?book_show_action=true">Apr 28, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bridget Mckinney" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bridget Mckinney" href="/user/show/6915631-bridget-mckinney">Bridget Mckinney</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780679889144" href="/book/show/883287.First_Test">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6915631-bridget-mckinney?shelf=2013">2013</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer602327878" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6328399698342444070"><p>Before starting to read the Protector of the Small quartet, I read that Kel was just another Alanna and that the books are basically Song of the Lioness all over again. I was actually okay with that going into this series, since I <em>love</em> Alanna and think that there are far worse things Kel could have been than just like her. I'm happy to report, however, that although there are similarities between Alanna and Kel, their experiences are extremely different and Kel's story expands upon and continues</p></span>
  <span id="freeText6328399698342444070" style="display:none"><p>Before starting to read the Protector of the Small quartet, I read that Kel was just another Alanna and that the books are basically Song of the Lioness all over again. I was actually okay with that going into this series, since I <em>love</em> Alanna and think that there are far worse things Kel could have been than just like her. I'm happy to report, however, that although there are similarities between Alanna and Kel, their experiences are extremely different and Kel's story expands upon and continues a lot of the themes that were present in Song of the Lioness.</p><br /><p>I <a href="http://existentialcrisisfactory.tumblr.com/post/49140337254/currently-reading-first-test" rel="nofollow noopener">wrote about this</a> a little bit already, but I have to reiterate it here because it makes me so happy. Kel has a lot more support than Alanna did, from her family as well as from people she meets when she goes into page training, but at the same time Kel faces a lot more active and targeted sexist bullying than Alanna did. Alanna disguised herself as a boy, which meant she had to live in constant fear of discovery, but Kel faces danger because she <em>isn't</em> hiding. </p><br /><p>Something that I find interesting about the contrast between these two different situations is the ways in which their coping mechanisms and strategies overlap and diverge. Both Alanna and Kel find women who are friendly to them, although Kel and Alanna are denied each others company so far, which makes me <em>rage</em>. Both girls deal with bullies as pages; however, Alanna's bully was personal while the bullying Kel faces is sexist and institutional. Both girls make friends among the other pages, finding older boys willing to help mentor them.</p><br /><p>Something I especially loved was that, while Alanna hid her gender successfully for years, Kel makes a point of wearing dresses when she can as a way to never let the boys and men she is surrounded by forget that she is a girl. I love this little bit of recognition that gender is a performance and that the choices we make about how to perform are intensely personal AND political. In some ways, Kel is even more of a trailblazer than Alanna, simply because she is trying to become a knight openly. Alanna may have opened the door a crack for Kel, but Kel is the first girl to try and go through that door <em>as a girl</em>.</p><br /><p>In a lot of ways, I think that <em>First Test</em> is a lot more successful as a feminist work than <em>Alanna: The First Adventure</em> was, although I think both books should be required reading for girls (and boys, ideally). I think that Kel's experiences are closer to the real life ways in which girls experience sexism, and that's a valuable thing for young people to read about. </p></span>
  <a data-text-id="6328399698342444070" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_754275903" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/754275903" />
    <a title="Cass" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5612909-cass"><img alt="Cass" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1317582102p2/5612909.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/754275903?book_show_action=true">Nov 01, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cass" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cass" href="/user/show/5612909-cass">Cass</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780679889144" href="/book/show/883287.First_Test">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5612909-cass?shelf=speculative-and-fantastic">speculative-and-fantastic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5612909-cass?shelf=childhood-nostalgia">childhood-nostalgia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5612909-cass?shelf=y-a-lit">y-a-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5612909-cass?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5612909-cass?shelf=mighty-woman">mighty-woman</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer754275903" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8568718984085491877">I recommend this book to two (not mutually exclusive) groups of people: kids who love Harry Potter and are looking for something to read next, and girls looking for a heroine who is not just a badass, but an Interesting Person to boot. <br/><br/>Review of entire series:<br/>I read this series so many times in my teenage years, I nearly wore out the library copy. I was never over-impressed with Pierce's writing, but Keladry's quiet strength got under my skin and fascinated me. So many literary heroines are more</span>
  <span id="freeText8568718984085491877" style="display:none">I recommend this book to two (not mutually exclusive) groups of people: kids who love Harry Potter and are looking for something to read next, and girls looking for a heroine who is not just a badass, but an Interesting Person to boot. <br /><br />Review of entire series:<br />I read this series so many times in my teenage years, I nearly wore out the library copy. I was never over-impressed with Pierce's writing, but Keladry's quiet strength got under my skin and fascinated me. So many literary heroines are more after the Alanna the Lioness mold: hot-tempered, outgoing, feisty. So as a quiet bookish girl, a heroine who was soft-spoken and even-tempered, and who was also an iron-willed warrior, was delightfully refreshing. <br /><br />Other stories may have done more to spark my imagination, but Keladry gave me something even my beloved Tolkien couldn't: an example of female strength, not just in fighting monsters or finding "true love," but in more difficult obstacles like prejudice and unfair disadvantages. She taught me that a girl doesn't have to be a fiery redhead with a temper to be brave, or disguise herself as a boy to prove herself as good as one. Quiet determination and a clear head can be even more effective. <br /><br />I know there are better examples of great women in literature, but this is the one who was there for me, so I'm grateful to her.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8568718984085491877" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4277413540012035854">This book changed my childhood. I had read stories about lady knights before--about women dressing as men, fighting the odds, and changing the world. But this story is different. Kel doesn't dress in drag, she doesn't hide herself, she doesn't try to change the world. She just wants to be a knight, and will do whatever it takes to achieve her goal. She is my number one female character in a YA novel, and that has not changed in a long long time.<br/><br/>I highly recommend this book to anyone and everyone</span>
  <span id="freeText4277413540012035854" style="display:none">This book changed my childhood. I had read stories about lady knights before--about women dressing as men, fighting the odds, and changing the world. But this story is different. Kel doesn't dress in drag, she doesn't hide herself, she doesn't try to change the world. She just wants to be a knight, and will do whatever it takes to achieve her goal. She is my number one female character in a YA novel, and that has not changed in a long long time.<br /><br />I highly recommend this book to anyone and everyone. To people who want to feel better about humanity, people who want female characters who are realistic and soulful, or just people who love knighthood, battles, and magic.<br /><br />A+++</span>

<div id="review_633641329" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/633641329" />
    <a title="Dorothea" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6638679-dorothea"><img alt="Dorothea" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1335630852p2/6638679.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/633641329?book_show_action=true">Jun 05, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dorothea" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dorothea" href="/user/show/6638679-dorothea">Dorothea</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer633641329" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10183543856540233728">(re-read on May 26, 2013, the occasion of this review)<br/><br/>May I say first that whoever thought this cover (trendily cropped photograph of a conventionally beautiful young woman with her lips parted and wearing some sort of floating veil) was an improvement over <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/photo/1045477.First_Test' rel='nofollow noopener'>this cover</a> (painting of a ten-year-old child with an androgynous haircut, looking out optimistically at the world through her black eye, holding a kitten and surrounded by little birds) should be smacked with their own portfolio?<br/><br/>Thank you.<br/><br/>All</span>
  <span id="freeText10183543856540233728" style="display:none">(re-read on May 26, 2013, the occasion of this review)<br /><br />May I say first that whoever thought this cover (trendily cropped photograph of a conventionally beautiful young woman with her lips parted and wearing some sort of floating veil) was an improvement over <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/photo/1045477.First_Test" rel="nofollow noopener">this cover</a> (painting of a ten-year-old child with an androgynous haircut, looking out optimistically at the world through her black eye, holding a kitten and surrounded by little birds) should be smacked with their own portfolio?<br /><br />Thank you.<br /><br />All right, despite the two-star rating I'm still awfully fond of Kel. Previously I've read all four books in a blur. I hope that if I read the rest again, I'll enjoy the series overall as much as I have before -- but I wasn't awfully impressed by <i>First Test</i> by itself.<br /><br />Maybe it was just too simplistic for me? Which is a silly problem to have with a short book about a ten-year-old.<br /><br />Kel has to deal with really nasty bullying, sexism from her peers and authority figures, separation from her family, uncertainty about her future, an exhausting daily schedule that would give me a nervous breakdown, and actual peril to her life. She survives all of these triumphantly, thanks to her stubborn determination, unusual skills learned earlier in her childhood, and the right friends.<br /><br />When I put it that way, <i>First Test</i> sounds like a really good book, and yeah, that's why we all read Tamora Pierce to begin with, right?<br /><br />Kel has a <i>much</i> easier time dealing with all of these things than I can imagine myself having. She's also, overall, better at everything than her peers. This makes sense in a lot of ways. Kel wants this life and is well suited for it (unlike imaginary-me-in-Tortall), and the first [x] person to successfully make it through a difficult program that was previously limited to [y] usually does have to be extra amazing at everything.<br /><br />But Kel's extra-amazing advantages distract a lot from what I'd like this book to be. Kel is learning to be a page and I wanted to read about her learning. <i>First Test</i> seems really to be about how Kel is already more than worthy to be a page and how some of the gatekeepers just don't see how special she is.<br /><br />My favorite parts are when we do see Kel learning and applying what she's learned, like when she gets better at <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[tilting <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. But there are a lot of times when she overcomes an obstacle with the unique attributes she began with -- when she <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[shows up the etiquette teacher by knowing everything about Yamani manners, because she grew up there as a diplomat's child <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, or when <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[some bullies' plans are defeated because they are attacked by a flock of sparrows whom Kel has, as a matter of course, befriended <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br /><br />There's another criticism I feel less ambivalent in making -- Pierce could have done a much better job with characters of color.<br /><br />Did she have to make the the Yamanis instantly recognizable as East Asian stand-ins by means of so many stereotypes? Why did she decide to give Kel so many advantages from growing up in Yamani society, yet make her a white Tortallan instead of actually a Yamani girl? It's not that children of other nationalities can't train as pages in Tortall, because there's another page who's a Bazhir boy. And that was another missed opportunity. Doesn't that kid also feel isolated because of his differences from the other pages? Wouldn't that make him a good friend for Kel? Instead, Pierce decided at some point that her Bazhir characters would share in this world's American stereotype of Middle Eastern men being extra specially sexist. So this character is one of the bullies, and in <i>First Test</i> at least, he has no depth to his character and no redeeming qualities at all.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10183543856540233728" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer774570460" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5649524230342550033">This review was written ages ago when I was in library school but I'm leaving it because I'm lazy. This millionth re-read was just as good as all the rest and I actually listened to it on audio this time so that made it just a little more fresh and new. I will be reading all of Pierce's books FOREVERRRRRRR. Also I laughed bc for some reason I like indented two of those paragraphs but I'm leaving it just because why not.<br/>---<br/>Keladry of Mindelan and her family have just come back to Tortall from a s</span>
  <span id="freeText5649524230342550033" style="display:none">This review was written ages ago when I was in library school but I'm leaving it because I'm lazy. This millionth re-read was just as good as all the rest and I actually listened to it on audio this time so that made it just a little more fresh and new. I will be reading all of Pierce's books FOREVERRRRRRR. Also I laughed bc for some reason I like indented two of those paragraphs but I'm leaving it just because why not.<br />---<br />Keladry of Mindelan and her family have just come back to Tortall from a six year diplomatic delegation stint in the Yamani Islands. One day after an attack from a group of spidrens (monster spiders) she decides it is time to begin her training as a lady knight. The only problem with that, is that there has not been a woman who has knowingly gone through training in at least a hundred years. The only reason she is able to do so now is because of the legendary Alanna, a woman who pretended to be a boy all throughout her training, alongside the current King. Although she is accepted, Kel is placed on probation on her first year, something that is never done with the boys and is completely unfair. Stubborn as she is though, she works harder than all of the boys and along with her best friend Neal and a few intelligent sparrows, she proves to training master Wyldon that she is worthy and deserving of becoming a page.<br /><br />	First Test is the first of Tamora Pierce’s Protector of the Small quartet and a great deal different than her previous eight books set in Tortall. Unlike Alanna, the first female knight in over a century, Kel goes into training as a girl. This means that essentially the entire kingdom is against her being there and will do anything in their power to make her leave including hazing, threats, rumors, etc. Luckily, Kel has spent a good portion of her time in the Yamani Islands (similar to Japan) and has gathered techniques to keep her calm and level headed under the most extreme and trying situations. I love that Pierce made Kel that way because even the reader still knew how upset or frustrated she was, she never let that be a weakness. Kel was able to prove time and time again that she worked as hard, if not probably a lot harder to become and stay better than all of the boys that were her year mates in page training.<br /><br />	Pierce’s writing style is so engaging and she has just done such an amazing job building this world of Tortall that I have grown to become so familiar with. I was glad that the four books were separated into the different years of Kel being on probation, a page, a squire, and then onto a lady knight. This allowed me as a reader to grow with Kel and be just as excited as she is when she earns respect and praise by hard work and determination. Pierce is my favorite author and is one of the most amazing writers of fantasy that I have ever read. Her characters, Kel especially, are exceptional and it’s so hard not to root for her because she’s such an awesome female [ass] kicker.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5649524230342550033" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2431901989" />
    <a title="Belinda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45524597-belinda"><img alt="Belinda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597434233p2/45524597.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Belinda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Belinda" href="/user/show/45524597-belinda">Belinda</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

<div id="review_1638384824" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1638384824" />
    <a title="Elaine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/55868018-elaine"><img alt="Elaine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1530510048p2/55868018.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1638384824?book_show_action=true">May 14, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elaine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elaine" href="/user/show/55868018-elaine">Elaine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55868018-elaine?shelf=favorite-books">favorite-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55868018-elaine?shelf=tamora-pierce-books">tamora-pierce-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1638384824" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5458670504309307806">I remember not liking this quartet very much when I first read it. I thought it was a less interesting retelling of Alanna’s quartet (which starts with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13831.Alanna_The_First_Adventure__Song_of_the_Lioness___1_' title='Alanna The First Adventure (Song of the Lioness, #1) by Tamora Pierce' rel='nofollow noopener'>Alanna: The First Adventure</a>), which is also by Tamora Pierce.<br/><br/>However, this series has grown on me over the years. It’s better written than Pierce's previous quartets, and the side characters are more fleshed out. Kel stills seems far too wise beyond her years to me, and her lack of emotion is annoying, especially in the earlier books. I don’t min</span>
  <span id="freeText5458670504309307806" style="display:none">I remember not liking this quartet very much when I first read it. I thought it was a less interesting retelling of Alanna’s quartet (which starts with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13831.Alanna_The_First_Adventure__Song_of_the_Lioness___1_" title="Alanna The First Adventure (Song of the Lioness, #1) by Tamora Pierce" rel="nofollow noopener">Alanna: The First Adventure</a>), which is also by Tamora Pierce.<br /><br />However, this series has grown on me over the years. It’s better written than Pierce's previous quartets, and the side characters are more fleshed out. Kel stills seems far too wise beyond her years to me, and her lack of emotion is annoying, especially in the earlier books. I don’t mind stoic heroes, but when the story is told from their perspective, we need to get a sense of what they are feeling internally, even if they keep a cool, outer shell.<br /><br />Kel wants to follow in Alanna's footsteps and become a lady knight. The king made a proclamation ten years ago that allows noble girls to train for their shield, but no one has come forward until Kel. The more conservative people at court think women should not be warriors. Kel sets out to prove herself to her fellow pages and those naysayers alike. <br /><br />I really think this book’s plot could have been condensed and included in the second book, Page, without losing anything. There is a little bit of drama because Wyldon might expel Kel after her probationary year, but I was never worried she would fail. Plus, Kel is at her worst here when it comes to masking her emotions. Judging on First Test alone, Kel would make a much better supporting character and friend than she does a main character.<br /><br />I also don't quite understand why so many nobles are against female knights. Tortall is a relatively progressive country. Alanna has been the King's Champion for many years, and she is a hero who is loved by many. The queen is a powerful woman who rules jointly with her husband. The Queen's Riders allow female members. The only force that doesn't allow women are the King's Own, which is silly anyways. Given all of that, it makes no sense why the prevailing attitude would be "women are too weak to be warriors."<br /><br />I did like that Kel did not have the magical Gift like Alanna or Wild Magic like Daine. She's a "normal" character instead of a hero blessed with extraordinary power. That type of person is not often the protagonist in a fantasy.<br /><br />Generally, each book in this series gets better and better. It's a great one for young girls and early teens filled with strong, likeable heroines. While I wasn't sure of it at first, this quartet has become one of my favorite series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5458670504309307806" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2895272832" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2895272832" />
    <a title="Alex Black" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42803361-alex-black"><img alt="Alex Black" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1578085065p2/42803361.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2895272832?book_show_action=true">Jul 14, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alex Black" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alex Black" href="/user/show/42803361-alex-black">Alex Black</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42803361-alex-black?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42803361-alex-black?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42803361-alex-black?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42803361-alex-black?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2895272832" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12991939923850369819">I remember never being quite as fond of the Protector of the Small series as I was the other Tortall books, particularly the two first ones, but as an adult, I thought it was absolutely brilliant. The premise of the series is that 14 years after Alanna, girls are allowed to become knights, but it's still a very sexist, patriarchal society, so no girl has. I really enjoyed that because it didn't just have Alanna fixing everything by being a heroic woman. She definitely changed the world a great d</span>
  <span id="freeText12991939923850369819" style="display:none">I remember never being quite as fond of the Protector of the Small series as I was the other Tortall books, particularly the two first ones, but as an adult, I thought it was absolutely brilliant. The premise of the series is that 14 years after Alanna, girls are allowed to become knights, but it's still a very sexist, patriarchal society, so no girl has. I really enjoyed that because it didn't just have Alanna fixing everything by being a heroic woman. She definitely changed the world a great deal, but didn't solve all of its problems.<br /><br />And Kel is a very different protagonist than Alanna. Alanna is a hero, a mythical figure almost with the gods on her side and powerful magic, coming from a long line of nobility. Kel is just an ordinary kid who wants to be knight like her older brothers, just like a hundred other kids in the country. She doesn't have magic, she doesn't have the gods on her side. She doesn't have lofty aspirations as a knight. She just wants to do her duty to her country. And it makes such an interesting contrast to Alanna, who has a strong presence in this book.<br /><br />One of my favorite things about this book is how heavily it deals with femininity. Kel has very little desire in typically feminine pursuits because they don't interest her, but when the other boys bully her and threaten her and tell her to go home, she doesn't try to blend in. She actively wears dresses whenever possible to make herself girly as a reminder that she's different and she's not ashamed of being a girl. I loved that element. I've read very little that's more badass than a female character sticking it to a patriarchal society by actively being more feminine.<br /><br />This book also deals more heavily with politics than the previous series in the Tortall universe, which I think is one reason I enjoyed it less as child, but I love it more for that now. The conservatives are fighting against many changes in the country, including female knights and fighters. Kel has little interest in politics, just wanting to be an ordinary knight, but she can't avoid it simply because she's a girl. It's an interesting element to the story, and really well done in this book.<br /><br />Overall, I'd highly recommend this series. I think it's definitely better to read it after Alanna because so much of the world building and the government and history comes from that series, but it has fewer problematic issues as it was written fifteen years later. I think this may become my favorite series in this universe, just based off the first book.<br /><br />(Tagged as YA for the series)</span>
  <a data-text-id="12991939923850369819" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
