<div id="review_1750886604" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1750886604" />
    <a title="Jackie B. - Death by Tsundoku" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8952328-jackie-b---death-by-tsundoku"><img alt="Jackie B. - Death by Tsundoku" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1484085383p2/8952328.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1750886604?book_show_action=true">Sep 06, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jackie B. - Death by Tsundoku" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jackie B. - Death by Tsundoku" href="/user/show/8952328-jackie-b---death-by-tsundoku">Jackie B. - Death by Tsundoku</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8952328-jackie-b---death-by-tsundoku?shelf=coming-of-age">coming-of-age</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8952328-jackie-b---death-by-tsundoku?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8952328-jackie-b---death-by-tsundoku?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8952328-jackie-b---death-by-tsundoku?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8952328-jackie-b---death-by-tsundoku?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1750886604" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12679315270826495822">Ten years after Alanna becomes King's Champion, a female of Tortall finally wants to become a page-- and eventually a knight of the realm. What sounds at first as a repeat of the Song of the Lioness quartet is quickly revealed to be much more. While our protagonist, Kelandry of Mindalen, is following the same path as Alanna, the road the walks is completely different. Tamora Pierce takes what could have been a copycat novel and turns a parallel story into something refreshing and new.<br/><br/>From the st</span>
  <span id="freeText12679315270826495822" style="display:none">Ten years after Alanna becomes King's Champion, a female of Tortall finally wants to become a page-- and eventually a knight of the realm. What sounds at first as a repeat of the Song of the Lioness quartet is quickly revealed to be much more. While our protagonist, Kelandry of Mindalen, is following the same path as Alanna, the road the walks is completely different. Tamora Pierce takes what could have been a copycat novel and turns a parallel story into something refreshing and new.<br /><br />From the start, we can see many parallels between Kel and Alanna's story. Both want to prove themselves, both are training to become knights, both have a quartet of books that follow progress from page to squire to knight, heck, both even have a member of the royal family on their side. Yet their stories are very different. Alanna hid her sex, was blessed by the Goddess, and has magical powers. Kel merely want to protect her country and has little more going for her. <br /><br />Infuriatingly, because of her sex, Kel is forced to undergo a "probationary period", which makes her more of a pariah with her fellow pages than she was going to be just by being a girl. In fact, Alanna was hoping to protect and train Kel as the first openly female page-- but she is forbidden. From the start, we know Kel will be subject to incredible sexism and abuse. Her journey, in many ways, is much harder than the one Alanna traveled. Kel must rely on her own strength, self-confidence, and determination to prove herself on this journey. <br /><br />In many ways, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/153784.First_Test__Protector_of_the_Small___1_" title="First Test (Protector of the Small, #1) by Tamora Pierce" rel="nofollow noopener">First Test</a> is a much stronger feminist statement than<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13831.Alanna_The_First_Adventure__Song_of_the_Lioness___1_" title="Alanna The First Adventure (Song of the Lioness, #1) by Tamora Pierce" rel="nofollow noopener">Alanna: The First Adventure</a>. It was written over a decade later, after all. I look forward to seeing how Alanna's sacrifices paved the way for the next generation of female warriors. After all, in reality gaining the right to vote didn't establish equality. I know Kel has a long way to go. I'll be with her all the way. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12679315270826495822" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2992877407" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2992877407" />
    <a title="Andrew" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4515370-andrew"><img alt="Andrew" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593978442p2/4515370.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2992877407?book_show_action=true">Oct 03, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andrew" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andrew" href="/user/show/4515370-andrew">Andrew</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780008304195" href="/book/show/52756713-first-test">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4515370-andrew?shelf=library-prime">library-prime</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4515370-andrew?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2992877407" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7011456871690167704">Can't decided between 3.5 stars or 4. I did like it, but this is very much a "starter" book. <br/><br/>THREE TIMES I HAVE TRIED TO PUT THIS REVIEW UP! THREE TIMES!!! grrr!!! <br/><br/>Review Taken from <a href='http://thepewterwolf.blogspot.com/2019/10/audiobook-review-first-test.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Pewter Wolf</a><br/><br/>Keladry of Mindelan is the first girl who dares to take advantage of the new law of Tortall, allowing females to train for Knighthood. After growing up on the Yamani Islands, she knows women can be fearless warriors and she wants to be one. But Lord Wyldon, the training master, is dead against the idea</span>
  <span id="freeText7011456871690167704" style="display:none">Can't decided between 3.5 stars or 4. I did like it, but this is very much a "starter" book. <br /><br />THREE TIMES I HAVE TRIED TO PUT THIS REVIEW UP! THREE TIMES!!! grrr!!! <br /><br />Review Taken from <a href="http://thepewterwolf.blogspot.com/2019/10/audiobook-review-first-test.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Pewter Wolf</a><br /><br />Keladry of Mindelan is the first girl who dares to take advantage of the new law of Tortall, allowing females to train for Knighthood. After growing up on the Yamani Islands, she knows women can be fearless warriors and she wants to be one. But Lord Wyldon, the training master, is dead against the idea of girls becoming knights and forces the king to say that Kel must do a year’s trial - something no boy has ever done. Kel is determined to prove herself, just to be seen as equal…<br /><br />This is the first book in the series so I am quite intrigued to see how the rest of the series moves forward. But the rest of the series isn’t on my library audiobook app, so I won’t know for quite some time what happens next. <br /><br />I did like this audiobook. I want to make that clear. It was a nice start to the fantasy series and I rooted for Kel. I think this is the set-up book as it’s letting us know the characters and put us in the right places and, hopefully, as the series moves forward, it gets bigger in scope and story-arc. <br /><br />I did have times listening to this audiobook where I did struggle. But I can’t figure out if I didn’t click with the narrator or if I felt uncomfortable with the level of sexism that Kel faces. And I think this is important as sexism, sadly, still does exist and it’s important that we see characters stand up and fight back against it. Plus, what shocked me was Kel and her classmates are ten or eleven years old, but the level of sexism issued at Kel disturbed me.<br /><br />I did like this book, and it made a nice change from the heavy “straight white male” fantasy that exists in the adult fantasy genre, but this is a starter book and, as the series goes on, I want more something a tad meatier. <br /><br />Or maybe I shouldn't mix my Tamora Pierce reading up - I have several ebooks on my kindle and eye several other audiobooks on my library audiobook app! Oh, whatever I decide to read next by her is going to really confuse my brain, isn't it? </span>
  <a data-text-id="7011456871690167704" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3614271772461522866">After King Jonathan took the throne, he decreed that women could train as knights as well. But more than a decade has passed since Alanna was unveiled as a female knight, and still no other female member of a noble house has come forth to be trained. No one--until Keladry. The daughter of ambassadors, Kel spent her childhood in lands where women were trained warriors, and intends to become one herself. Jonathon's hide-bound nobles aren't pleased with this change of tradition, and to placate them</span>
  <span id="freeText3614271772461522866" style="display:none">After King Jonathan took the throne, he decreed that women could train as knights as well. But more than a decade has passed since Alanna was unveiled as a female knight, and still no other female member of a noble house has come forth to be trained. No one--until Keladry. The daughter of ambassadors, Kel spent her childhood in lands where women were trained warriors, and intends to become one herself. Jonathon's hide-bound nobles aren't pleased with this change of tradition, and to placate them, Jonathan agrees that Kel will be merely a <em>probationary</em> page, subject to being tossed out at her first failure. <br /><br />Kel, however, is too damn awesome for that crap. She's the kind of person who, when she discovers her lance has been unfairly weighted with lead, keeps training with the weighted lance in order to become stronger. No matter what they throw at her, she rises to the challenge. <br /><br />This book was so much fun to read! Energizing and inspiring and thrilling--altogether my favorite kind of wish-fullfillment fantasy.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5590004602029896326">This and my other reviews can be found at <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://amethystbookwyrm.blogspot.co.uk/'>http://amethystbookwyrm.blogspot.co.uk/</a><br/><br/>First Test is about Keladry of Mindelan, the first girl who wishes to become a knight since Lady Alanna. She has been accepted for knight training, however, unlike the boys she will study and train beside, she has been given a First Test, one year to prove to the conservative training master that she is able to withstand the rigors of page training.<br/><br/>The storyline of this book progresses in a very good yet predictable</span>
  <span id="freeText5590004602029896326" style="display:none">This and my other reviews can be found at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://amethystbookwyrm.blogspot.co.uk/">http://amethystbookwyrm.blogspot.co.uk/</a><br /><br />First Test is about Keladry of Mindelan, the first girl who wishes to become a knight since Lady Alanna. She has been accepted for knight training, however, unlike the boys she will study and train beside, she has been given a First Test, one year to prove to the conservative training master that she is able to withstand the rigors of page training.<br /><br />The storyline of this book progresses in a very good yet predictable way. There are boys who try to force Keladry to leave through bullying her, and there are her staunch and stalwart friends. She also befriends the animals, which have become smart since Daine came to live at the palace in the Immortals series.<br /><br />I like this book because it gives you the opportunity to see characters we have grown to love, from previous series, as they are when they have grown up. <br /><br />I would recommend First Test to anyone who likes the rest of Tamora Pierce’s books, or well written fantasy books.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1379023830" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15653832087727633258">I would've devoured this at age 10 or so. Now, I'm less interested in stories where women have to prove themselves to men. That's right. I'm embracing my inner Carol Danvers. That said, I loved Kel and Neil and their friendship, and this was a fast, fun listen. I would've given it four stars, except I'm not into stories where the big bad is a monstrous/non-human species. Just personal preference.<br/><br/>Definitely a book/series I'll give my niece and nephew when they're old enough.</span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9861038438375173648">Every time I reread this book, I find myself loving it even more. From Kel and Neal's unlikely friendship to her stalwart, solid sense of loyalty and justice, I could probably reread this series every month and not grow tired of it. <br/><br/>Plus, nothing sends me to tears quicker than Kel peeling into a hallway shouting to her friends that she can stay for the rest of their training.<br/><br/><br/>edit from Nov. 2016: I have apparently reached the "read Kel's books twice a year" stage.   <span id="freeText9861038438375173648" style="display:none">Every time I reread this book, I find myself loving it even more. From Kel and Neal's unlikely friendship to her stalwart, solid sense of loyalty and justice, I could probably reread this series every month and not grow tired of it. <br /><br />Plus, nothing sends me to tears quicker than Kel peeling into a hallway shouting to her friends that she can stay for the rest of their training.<br /><br /><br />edit from Nov. 2016: I have apparently reached the "read Kel's books twice a year" stage. I... needed the encouragement after the election, and Kel (and Tammy) came through. What a beautiful picture of resilience and determination--as well as of friendship and hope and hard work.<br /><br />update from June 2017: Keladry and Neal remain the best and yes, I still cried after reading the ending. For the twentieth or whatever time this is. </span>

    <a title="Ashley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2379139-ashley"><img alt="Ashley" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

<span id="freeTextContainer5741591844909871602">I am very excited because my big reread has finally gotten to the Kel books, and Kel is my *FAVORITE* Tamora Pierce heroine. She doesn't have magic powers, so she gets everything done on her own. She's stubborn, she works incredibly hard, and she always stands up to a bully. I also have always loved Neal and his dramatics, even though this time around I couldn't help wondering, what kind of 15-year-old is perfectly happy to spend so much time with 10 to 13-year-olds? Doesn't he ever want to talk</span>
  <span id="freeText5741591844909871602" style="display:none">I am very excited because my big reread has finally gotten to the Kel books, and Kel is my *FAVORITE* Tamora Pierce heroine. She doesn't have magic powers, so she gets everything done on her own. She's stubborn, she works incredibly hard, and she always stands up to a bully. I also have always loved Neal and his dramatics, even though this time around I couldn't help wondering, what kind of 15-year-old is perfectly happy to spend so much time with 10 to 13-year-olds? Doesn't he ever want to talk about teenager things? How old are the others in their group? But this isn't Neal's book, so I'll just let it go and assume he has a life and friends his own age that Kel just doesn't know or think about. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5741591844909871602" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

Will review properly later when I don't have a detailed essay (on the use of moving image/film as an art form to explore social media and psychosis) to conclude.<br/><br/>Came across my 2003 school reading log, and I think my ten-year-old self actually describes this book best. In my own ten-year-old words: "Excellent, I like the idea that girls are at <u>least</u> as good as boys, if not better!"</span>

  <span id="freeText15788483594703096066" style="display:none">Five characters mentioned in the first sentence. Clearly this is not intended for people ignorant of the earlier series. After the third restart, I had to sit still and do that, just to track the sentence. Of Course, Tamora is on Overdrive like black on wild rice, so maybe she writes these in her sleep. You would think such a prolific writer might warrant a Beta reader, or an editor, but apparently not.</span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('iOIKNNZid3vc5cPaKIg6chJ6FMg1d5RJ+4nMZzMUohdAE634ACdqyOpByPNWHu6gXuo7i1Lw+TuOa+tzIBZslA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('XSB8MCx/V3qWZ4V7V6gz5XZmI0qDTQtsE9tnBj0401+V0dv8+jpKyaDDjlIpPuc3OvYMCeTKZh5mOUASLjod3A==')})
  }
//]]>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/8596.Tamora_Pierce">About Tamora Pierce</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/8596.Tamora_Pierce"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1209044273p3/8596.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/8596.Tamora_Pierce">Tamora Pierce
</a></div>
<div class='goodreadsAuthorBadge'></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
81,367
followers

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer16703059652033916343">Hey, folks! I just discovered that apparently I have given some very popular books single-star ratings--except I haven't. How do I know I haven't? Because I haven't read those books at all. So before you go getting all hacked off at me for trashing your favorites, know that I've written GoodReads to find out what's going on.<br/><br/>I return to my regularly scheduled profile:<br/>Though I would love to join gro</span>
  <span id="freeText16703059652033916343" style="display:none">Hey, folks! I just discovered that apparently I have given some very popular books single-star ratings--except I haven't. How do I know I haven't? Because I haven't read those books at all. So before you go getting all hacked off at me for trashing your favorites, know that I've written GoodReads to find out what's going on.<br /><br />I return to my regularly scheduled profile:<br />Though I would love to join groups, I'm going to turn them all down. I just don't have the time to take part, so please don't be offended if I don't join your group or accept an invitation. I'm not snooty--I'm just up to my eyeballs in work and appearances!<br /><br />Also, don't be alarmed by the number of books I've read. When I get bored, I go through the different lists and rediscover books I've read in the past. It's a very evil way to use up time when I should be doing other things. Obviously, I've read a lot of books in 54 years!<br /><br />I was born in South Connellsville, PA. My mother wanted to name me "Tamara" but the nurse who filled out my birth certificate misspelled it as "Tamora". When I was 8 my family moved to California, where we lived for 6 years on both sides of the San Francisco peninsula.<br /><br />I started writing stories in 6th grade. My interest in fantasy and science fiction began when I was introduced to ‘The Lord of the Rings’ by J. R. R. Tolkien and so I started to write the kind of books that I was reading. After my parents divorced, my mother took my sisters and me back to Pennsylvania in 1969. There I went to Albert Gallatin Senior High for 2 years and Uniontown Area Senior High School for my senior year.<br /><br />After graduating from the University of Pennsylvania, I wrote the book that became The Song of the Lioness fantasy quartet. I sold some articles and 2 short stories and wrote reviews for a martial arts movie magazine. At last the first book of the quartet, Alanna: The First Adventure was published by Atheneum Books in 1983.<br /><br />Tim Liebe, who became my Spouse-Creature, and I lived in New York City with assorted cats and two parakeets from 1982 - 2006. In 2006 we moved to Syracuse, New York, where we live now with assorted cats, a number of squirrels, birds, raccoons, skunks, opossums, and woodchucks visiting our very small yard. As of 2011, I have 27 novels in print, one short story collection, one comic book arc ("White Tiger: A Hero's Compulsion") co-written with Tim, and a short story anthology co-editing credit. There's more to come, including a companion book to the Tortall `verse. So stay tuned!</span>
  <a data-text-id="16703059652033916343" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>

Never one to rest on her laurels, Kel champs a<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText11865786766468052140\" style=\"display:none\">In the final thrilling installment of Tamora Pierce\'s Protector of the Small series ( First Test, Page, and Squire), our sturdy young heroine, Keladry of Mindelan (a.k.a. Kel), has finally been knighted. Never one to rest on her laurels, Kel champs at the bit, ready to tackle the horrific magic killing devices she was shown in the Chamber of the Ordeal during her knighthood initiation. The huge, insectlike machines, &quot;made of iron-coated giants\' bones, chains, pulleys, dagger-fingers and -toes, and a long whiplike tail,&quot; feed on the souls of dead children and are systematically killing off the citizens and warriors of Tortall.  Thoroughly disgusted to discover that not only is she not going to be assigned a combat post, but she has been placed in charge of a refugee camp instead, Kel, in her usual noble, stoic way, swallows her disappointment and sets out being the best refugee camp commander possible. Of course, destiny has a way of sneaking up on a young woman like Kel, and soon she is fulfilling the ordeal the Chamber set out for her... and then some. Tamora Pierce once again draws her legions of fans into her story, blending humor, pathos, exhilarating battles, and gripping drama with a very real, very appealing protagonist. It\'s easy to make war appear black and white, a matter of good versus evil. Pierce finds the shades of gray. (Ages 12 and older) --Emilie Coulter<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"11865786766468052140\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));; return false;\">...more<\/a>\n\n    <\/div>\n\n      <div
